<span id="freeTextContainer9665131653114067480">Kate Malvern, rescued from penury by her aunt Minerva, finds the grand household at Staplewood very unhomelike — even family dinners are formal. When she begins to suspect the shocking reason for Minerva’s generosity, there is no one to confide in.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1116983390">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1116983390" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/17861817-ruth-turner" class="left imgcol" title="Ruth Turner"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1435387851p2/17861817.jpg" alt="Ruth Turner" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1116983390?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 28, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/17861817-ruth-turner" class="user" title="Ruth Turner">Ruth Turner</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311189.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780099490951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/17861817-ruth-turner?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1116983390">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7848212487696425957"><br />The romance was really a side issue in this book, with none of the feeling that Georgette Heyer has imbued in her other Regency Romances. The love story developed way too quickly and I thought Philip and Kate rather insipid.<br /><br />However, apart from the romance, this was a good read, and I have to say that I loved old Mr Nid. His conversations were priceless!<br /></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4388626469779412493">The one where penniless, orphaned Kate is taken in by an aunt she's never met, and begins to discover strange things happening in the manor. <br /><br />This was two different books that didn't mesh well together. The romance conflicts with the suspense in a way that takes the power out of both of them. By the time Kate finds out she could be in real danger, she's already got an ally who's more powerful than any of the forces that threaten her. And in a romance context I accept women agreeing to marry men t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4388626469779412493">The one where penniless, orphaned Kate is taken in by an aunt she's never met, and begins to discover strange things happening in the manor. <br /><br />This was two different books that didn't mesh well together. The romance conflicts with the suspense in a way that takes the power out of both of them. By the time Kate finds out she could be in real danger, she's already got an ally who's more powerful than any of the forces that threaten her. And in a romance context I accept women agreeing to marry men they've only known for a week, but in a suspense context -- in a book that keeps whispering, <em>people are not what they appear; people who seem to be kind are dangerous</em> -- it seemed like a crazy thing to do. <br /><br />Well, OK, not really; in reality, you could identify the good guys and the bad guys within five minutes of meeting them, but that just means that the suspense-novel rules applied to the bad guys and the romance-novel rules applied to the good ones.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12620461289286395696"><strong>I've given this a B for narration and a B- for content at AudioGals.</strong><br /><br />If you pick up <strong>Cousin Kate</strong> expecting to listen to one of Georgette Heyer’s trademark romantic comedies of manners, then I’m afraid you might be a little disappointed, as this book is somewhat of a departure from her usual vein.<br /><br /><strong>Cousin Kate</strong> is more of a gothic mystery than a romance (although there is one), in which the orphaned Kate Malvern is taken in by her aunt, only to discover that there is perhaps more to that lady’s motive</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12620461289286395696"><strong>I've given this a B for narration and a B- for content at AudioGals.</strong><br /><br />If you pick up <strong>Cousin Kate</strong> expecting to listen to one of Georgette Heyer’s trademark romantic comedies of manners, then I’m afraid you might be a little disappointed, as this book is somewhat of a departure from her usual vein.<br /><br /><strong>Cousin Kate</strong> is more of a gothic mystery than a romance (although there is one), in which the orphaned Kate Malvern is taken in by her aunt, only to discover that there is perhaps more to that lady’s motives than simple generosity.<br /><br />Kate is twenty-four, and at the beginning of the story has just returned to London following her dismissal from a post as governess because one of the young men in the household couldn’t keep his hands to himself. Having followed the drum for more than half her life, she has no airs or graces about her, even though she’s a well-born young lady – which is just as well because when her father died, leaving her with nothing, she had to make her own way in life. In London, she stays at the home of Sarah Nidd, her former nurse, who is outraged at Kate’s latest idea of trying to find herself work as a ladies maid, which is, in Sarah’s opinion, no occupation for a young lady of quality.<br /><br />You can read the rest of this review at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.audiogals.net/2014/11/cousin-kate-by-georgette-heyer/"></a>AudioGals<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_220729938">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/220729938" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4181111-kathryn" class="left imgcol" title="Kathryn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1320032014p2/4181111.jpg" alt="Kathryn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/220729938?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 08, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4181111-kathryn" class="user" title="Kathryn">Kathryn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311189.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780099490951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4181111-kathryn?shelf=gothic" class="actionLinkLite">gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer220729938">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9218570135204580069"><em>Cousin Kate</em> was quite a surprise to me the first time I read it; I was expecting a light and fluffy Regency romance but instead got a Gothic romance. For those who are unfamiliar with the term, Gothic romances are a subset of romance novels that feature heroines going through all sorts of dreadful adventures, including fire, flood, ghosts, murderers, skeletons, etc., before finally finding the right man. These novels were extremely popular with young English women during the Regency era, but mos</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9218570135204580069"><em>Cousin Kate</em> was quite a surprise to me the first time I read it; I was expecting a light and fluffy Regency romance but instead got a Gothic romance. For those who are unfamiliar with the term, Gothic romances are a subset of romance novels that feature heroines going through all sorts of dreadful adventures, including fire, flood, ghosts, murderers, skeletons, etc., before finally finding the right man. These novels were extremely popular with young English women during the Regency era, but most haven’t survived to today (although you can find, for example, <em>The Mysteries of Udolpho</em> at Project Gutenberg). But a contemporary reader can still get the idea; <em>Jane Eyre</em> is (sort of) a Gothic romance, including classic features like the confined mad wife and the dread conflagration, and <em>Northanger Abbey</em> is a pastiche of the more outrageous of these books.<br /><br />At any rate, to be expecting light banter and instead get mystery and a wee spice of adventure is quite a surprise. That being said, however, I really enjoyed <em>Cousin Kate</em> and have enjoyed it more on subsequent rereads. The heroine is appealing and likeable, and the hero is pleasant likewise (if a tiny bit generic in that he resembles many other Heyer Heroes). Sadly, we don’t get that many scenes with the two of them, but the ones we do get are quite good.<br /><br />The story opens with the titular Kate, an orphan, returning to the arms of her old nurse after having lost her position as a governess due to the advances of her employer’s brother-in-law. Kate is too young and pretty to make a good governess in homes with susceptible young men; she grows quite despondent as, under her nurse Sarah’s aegis, she continues to search for work. Sarah has a much more refined idea of what work is appropriate for a young lady of quality such as her Kate, and in desperation, writes to one of Kate’s sole remaining relatives. (Her parents having made an imprudent marriage, the majority of her relatives have cast her completely off.) Lady Broome, Kate’s half-aunt, arrives to carry Kate off to her gloomy old mansion, Staplewood, which is tenanted by the ancient Sir Timothy Broome, Lady Broome, their young and wilful son Torquil, the slimy Dr. Delabole, and – of course – a dreadful secret.<br /><br />When I read the book for the first time, by the time I realized I was reading a Gothic romance instead of a Regency one, I was already quite close to puzzling out the mystery, and throughly enjoyed the book. I highly recommend it to anyone who likes romance of this style.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9218570135204580069">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_268156446">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/268156446" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim" class="left imgcol" title="Olga Godim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442639299p2/7438487.jpg" alt="Olga Godim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/268156446?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 23, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7438487-olga-godim" class="user" title="Olga Godim">Olga Godim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311189.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780099490951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7438487-olga-godim?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer268156446">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9896879215736024925">Unlike most Heyer’s romances, which are light-hearted romps, this novel is sad, almost tragic, with a brooding atmosphere of Gothic horror and a cast of characters to match. <br />The protagonist Kate is a penniless young woman of twenty-four. Her parents are dead, she doesn’t have any other relatives, and the only person who loves her is her former nurse. Kicked out from her position as a governess, Kate is trying in vain to find a new ‘situation’. She is close to despair, when unexpectedly a rich Au</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9896879215736024925">Unlike most Heyer’s romances, which are light-hearted romps, this novel is sad, almost tragic, with a brooding atmosphere of Gothic horror and a cast of characters to match. <br />The protagonist Kate is a penniless young woman of twenty-four. Her parents are dead, she doesn’t have any other relatives, and the only person who loves her is her former nurse. Kicked out from her position as a governess, Kate is trying in vain to find a new ‘situation’. She is close to despair, when unexpectedly a rich Aunt Minerva appears and sweeps Kate into her majestic country home. <br />Ambitious and autocratic, Minerva plies Kate with material gifts: new gowns, pearls, and shawls. Unused to the life of wealth and luxury, Kate is “crushed” by Minerva’s pointed generosity; it makes her uneasy. Wondering about her aunt’s hidden motives but trying to feel grateful, Kate navigates the complex currents of Minerva’s family. It includes the only son Torguil, a beautiful youth of nineteen with violent mood swings, a mysterious doctor, a frail uncle, and the uncle’s nephew Philip, who dislikes Kate on sight. <br />The action, slow and ponderous, with ominous undertones, takes place in Minerva’s large house. There are too many lengthy inner monologues, sometimes occupying a couple of pages, as the plot is based mostly on what happens in people’s heads, not on their physical movements. <br />Matrimonial schemes and concealed madness, family secrets and inexplicably disappearing letters make for a creepy tale of sorrow and deception, and the love story of Kate and Philip seems out of place in the spooky old house. Always in the background, subdued by the misfortunes of the house other occupants, this love story is undeveloped and sudden. One moment, it springs up fully formed and it feels like an afterthought, thrown in by the author to lighten the atmosphere.<br />The antagonist Minerva, on the other hand, is meticulously developed: a ruthless woman driven by her obsession, she is an evil force propelling the plot. <br />I wouldn’t call this story a romance, more like a psychological study in a literary frame. It was an intriguing read all the same and it kept me interested till the end.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9896879215736024925">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_715932251">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/715932251" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2974294-jessica" class="left imgcol" title="Jessica"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1281726456p2/2974294.jpg" alt="Jessica" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/715932251?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 11, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2974294-jessica" class="user" title="Jessica">Jessica</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311189.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780099490951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2974294-jessica?shelf=gothic" class="actionLinkLite">gothic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer715932251">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13878648626408813448">This book... I don't know, man. <br /><br />It has a Modern Gothic feel and a Regency Gothic setting, with its grand old house that becomes a mark of obsession for the innocent-but-plucky heroine's long-lost aunt (who reminded me greatly of Maleficent). Plus all sorts of family dysfunction and madness for extra Gothic fun. And it was definitely scary in places, in a small animals in danger from a proto-serial killer way. But the romance was very abrupt -- to the point where the heroine's suspicion that the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13878648626408813448">This book... I don't know, man. <br /><br />It has a Modern Gothic feel and a Regency Gothic setting, with its grand old house that becomes a mark of obsession for the innocent-but-plucky heroine's long-lost aunt (who reminded me greatly of Maleficent). Plus all sorts of family dysfunction and madness for extra Gothic fun. And it was definitely scary in places, in a small animals in danger from a proto-serial killer way. But the romance was very abrupt -- to the point where the heroine's suspicion that the hero was asking her to be his mistress rather than his wife seemed completely reasonable to me, and the story didn't seem very cohesive. Also, the heroine was... I don't know how to explain this exactly, but below is my impression of a few pivotal scenes.<br /><br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[<br /><br /><u>Torquil:</u> Hahaha, pretty cousin, I'm going to strangle you! *grabs her neck*<br /><u>Kate:</u> No, you're not. *smiles prettily*<br /><u>Torquil:</u> Yes, no, maybe *dither*<br /><u>Philip:</u> Unhand her!<br /><u>Torquil:</u> I wasn't going to kill her, she's too pretty.<br /><u>Kate:</u> Philip, why are you so upset? He's just a silly boy being silly.<br /><br /><br /><u>Kate:</u> Oh, I wonder what happened to that poor tortured bunny. And gee, Torquil's horse seems very nervous around him. Oh, what a pretty puppy! We don't see many dogs around here for some strange reason.<br /><u>Torquil:</u> Dog! Must kill it with the shotgun I stole from a locked room!<br /><u>Kate:</u> Torquil, you had no reason to shoot that poor dog! Or threaten to shoot your servant! Or almost shoot me, but that's beside the point. Oh, silly boy being silly. You should go home now and take a nap.<br /><br /><u>Kate:</u> Well, I know he's repeatedly threatened to kill me. And the servants and animals seem terrified of him. But his mother is trying to force me into marrying him even though he's my younger cousin which is squicky. So obviously she can't suspect that he's mad, even though she desperately wants an heir to maintain Staplewood, which is her one true love. But I refuse to believe that she'd deliberately marry me to a madman, because that would be mean and he's just a silly boy being silly.<br /><u>Philip:</u> okay?<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[<br /><br />Overall, the Gothic parts were probably the strongest part of the story, but I'm not keen on serial killer stuff and even for a Heyer adventure, the romance element seemed to come out of no-where. I am quite honestly unsure whether the problems I had with this were due to the flow of the story, with everything not quite blending together properly, or if I had trouble getting past what I expected a Heyer story to be.<br /><br />Not my favorite Heyer, but I think I may want to read it again in a few years, now that I have a better idea what to expect. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13878648626408813448">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_59139151">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/59139151" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1740420-christina" class="left imgcol" title="Christina"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1297548435p2/1740420.jpg" alt="Christina" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/59139151?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 12, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1740420-christina" class="user" title="Christina">Christina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6416850-cousin-kate" title="Paperback 9781402217685" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1740420-christina?shelf=2009-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2009-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1740420-christina?shelf=crime" class="actionLinkLite">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer59139151">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10632927520845349794">I put off reading Cousin Kate for almost three months now because False Colours and parts of A Convenient Marriage left a sour taste in my mouth. I actually started this book twice and barely managed to get past the first ten pages; the narrative just didn’t grabbed me. And then when I finally managed to plow through and start to the enjoy the story, the plot begins to lose it’s way. It deviates and takes roads that lead to no where, which ultimately means the story stutters and stalls at the en</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10632927520845349794">I put off reading Cousin Kate for almost three months now because False Colours and parts of A Convenient Marriage left a sour taste in my mouth. I actually started this book twice and barely managed to get past the first ten pages; the narrative just didn’t grabbed me. And then when I finally managed to plow through and start to the enjoy the story, the plot begins to lose it’s way. It deviates and takes roads that lead to no where, which ultimately means the story stutters and stalls at the end.<br /><br />I think part of my difficulty with Cousin Kate is the fact that it’s two different books — a romance novel and a mystery novel — forced together. Both aspects lack any sort of power over the narrative meaning that they cancel one another out. I was supposed to feel like Kate was in real danger, but by the time she (and I) realize how danger she actually was in, she had already found a powerful, stronger-than-the-danger man to save her. And, as someone else pointed out, I found utterly ridiculous that Kate would marry a men she’s only known for a week when people are not what they appear.<br /><br />I thought the most interesting part of Cousin Kate was the expose on the treatment of mental illness during the Regency period, but the ending almost voided out that for me. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10632927520845349794">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/4869211-meredith" class="left imgcol" title="Meredith"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1373380604p2/4869211.jpg" alt="Meredith" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/451336908?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 08, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4869211-meredith" class="user" title="Meredith">Meredith</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2994583-cousin-kate" title="Hardcover " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4869211-meredith?shelf=romantic-suspense-gothic-romance" class="actionLinkLite">romantic-suspense-gothic-romance</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/4869211-meredith?shelf=regency-romance" class="actionLinkLite">regency-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer451336908'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer451336908">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16578513755447108899">Sort of a halfway house between Heyer's standard regency romance and a more gothic style. This includes more violence than any other Heyer novel I've read. The moral to the story is: be suspicious of long-lost aunts who appear as fairy godmothers. <br /><br />It is more interesting for its discussion of insanity in a previous era. The reader is much quicker to pick up on indications Torquil has got some serious mental health issues (at a guess, maybe paranoid schizophrenia, multiple personality disorder, so</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16578513755447108899">Sort of a halfway house between Heyer's standard regency romance and a more gothic style. This includes more violence than any other Heyer novel I've read. The moral to the story is: be suspicious of long-lost aunts who appear as fairy godmothers. <br /><br />It is more interesting for its discussion of insanity in a previous era. The reader is much quicker to pick up on indications Torquil has got some serious mental health issues (at a guess, maybe paranoid schizophrenia, multiple personality disorder, some sort of psychopathy) than the protagonists. This is due not only to the greater awareness people in general now have about these matters but also the serious implications in that time of diagnosing and treating someone with mental health problems, or even worse, ruining their reputation wrongly if it turned out they were merely eccentric or bad-tempered!<br /><br />The main characters are much less interesting than the finely drawn portraits of working class Mr Nibb and his daughter-in-law Sarah, the mad bad and dangerous to know Lady Broome, and her husband, the ancient, ill and weak willed Sir Timothy. <br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16578513755447108899">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_53652967">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53652967" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1699270-kristi-books-and-needlepoint" class="left imgcol" title="Kristi (Books and Needlepoint)"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1238982375p2/1699270.jpg" alt="Kristi (Books and Needlepoint)" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/53652967?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 14, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1699270-kristi-books-and-needlepoint" class="user" title="Kristi (Books and Needlepoint)">Kristi (Books and Needlepoint)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/6416850-cousin-kate" title="Paperback 9781402217685" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer53652967">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12596553422878810631">Kate is a young girl in her mid-twenties. Young by our standards, but in the Regency period she was bordering on being an old maid. What is worse is that both of her parents have died, and she has just lost her job as a nanny. So she has no home, no job, and nothing for a dowry.<br /><br />She has traveled to her childhood nurse, Sarah's home until she can find another placement. She doesn't feel like she can stay with Sarah as she has her own husband and family to care for - so when her Aunt Minerva shows</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12596553422878810631">Kate is a young girl in her mid-twenties. Young by our standards, but in the Regency period she was bordering on being an old maid. What is worse is that both of her parents have died, and she has just lost her job as a nanny. So she has no home, no job, and nothing for a dowry.<br /><br />She has traveled to her childhood nurse, Sarah's home until she can find another placement. She doesn't feel like she can stay with Sarah as she has her own husband and family to care for - so when her Aunt Minerva shows up (her deceased father's estranged half-sister) - Kate views her as her salvation.<br /><br />Aunt Minerva, however, is not taking Kate home to Staplewood out of the goodness of her heart. She definitely has ulterior motives. She is looking for a wife for her son Torquil - and Torquil isn't exactly a "catch". Can Kate discover what her Aunt Minerva is up to before it is too late? And will her cousin Phillip be her ally?<br /><br />My thoughts: Where this wasn't necessarily a romance like the previous two Heyer books (A Convenient Marriage, Frederica) that I enjoyed - it wasn't really a mystery either like Why Shoot a Butler? which I didn't really care for at all. But no matter, I still liked this one. It contained all the humor and wit that I have come to expect when reading one of her novels.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12596553422878810631">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311189.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780099490951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8956777-lafleurbleue?shelf=romance-histo" class="actionLinkLite">romance-histo</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/8956777-lafleurbleue?shelf=e-book" class="actionLinkLite">e-book</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer370466097">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7441547660087402696">The gothic-reeking beginning of the book with Kate being smothered at Staplewood in a lurid environment full of hidden secrets, screams at night, weird characters took me by surprise but did not manage to engage me. It all seemed too much and Kate frequently seemed like a good-willing but slightly stupid goose to me.<br />Finally after more than 80 pages, the hero appeared on stage. He was as boring and colorless as the poor Cousin Kate. First they seemed to hate each other, then no longer. Their roma</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7441547660087402696">The gothic-reeking beginning of the book with Kate being smothered at Staplewood in a lurid environment full of hidden secrets, screams at night, weird characters took me by surprise but did not manage to engage me. It all seemed too much and Kate frequently seemed like a good-willing but slightly stupid goose to me.<br />Finally after more than 80 pages, the hero appeared on stage. He was as boring and colorless as the poor Cousin Kate. First they seemed to hate each other, then no longer. Their romance from then on was rather sweet and more demonstrative than in many other Heyer's books - they indeed kissed several times! I rather enjoyed Philip's proposal to Kate and the way she completely misunderstood his intentions.<br />However the mystery behind Torquil's condition and his mother's mastering of him took over the romance and was solved in a much more gory way than what I expected.<br />Certainly not one book I'll read again hoping for a light-hearted and fun entertainment!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7441547660087402696">...more</a>

          </span>

          <a href="/book/show/6416850-cousin-kate" title="Paperback 9781402217685" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1709540-debbie?shelf=historical" class="actionLinkLite">historical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1709540-debbie?shelf=romance" class="actionLinkLite">romance</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer952626849">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1636468342901637153">"Cousin Kate" is a Gothic Regency romance. It's got the screams in the night, locked doors, manipulations, and Gothic-style madness. Though not a light-hearted story, it's like Heyer couldn't let the story descend into a creepy or horror story--just some tense moments full of threat. Which is fine by me! The ending was very sad, but I felt like the author was trying too hard to convince the reader that this really was a happy ending. Also, since Kate is supposed to be world-traveled and not a sh</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1636468342901637153">"Cousin Kate" is a Gothic Regency romance. It's got the screams in the night, locked doors, manipulations, and Gothic-style madness. Though not a light-hearted story, it's like Heyer couldn't let the story descend into a creepy or horror story--just some tense moments full of threat. Which is fine by me! The ending was very sad, but I felt like the author was trying too hard to convince the reader that this really was a happy ending. Also, since Kate is supposed to be world-traveled and not a sheltered miss, I was baffled by how long it took her to even suspect what was wrong at Staplewood.<br /><br />There was no sex and no detailed descriptions of gory aspects. There was a fair amount of bad language (almost all of it the swearing use of "God"). Overall, this isn't my type of story, but others may enjoy it.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1289415118">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1289415118" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/406207-adobe" class="left imgcol" title="Adobe"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Adobe" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1289415118?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 25, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/406207-adobe" class="user" title="Adobe">Adobe</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311189.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780099490951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1289415118">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4729615955231212535">Penniless Kate Malvern is invited to visit her rich relations at Staplewood, a sprawling ancestral estate. But does Aunt Minerva have an ulterior motive in hosting Kate? And does something hidden lurk behind Cousin Torquil's handsome face?<br /><br /><em>Cousin Kate</em> is Georgette Heyer's attempt to write a Gothic novel chockablock full of locked doors, mutilated animals, and mad relatives. It lacks any of the daft characters or screwball humor from Heyer's earlier Regencies; instead, it is Very Very Serious. But</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4729615955231212535">Penniless Kate Malvern is invited to visit her rich relations at Staplewood, a sprawling ancestral estate. But does Aunt Minerva have an ulterior motive in hosting Kate? And does something hidden lurk behind Cousin Torquil's handsome face?<br /><br /><em>Cousin Kate</em> is Georgette Heyer's attempt to write a Gothic novel chockablock full of locked doors, mutilated animals, and mad relatives. It lacks any of the daft characters or screwball humor from Heyer's earlier Regencies; instead, it is Very Very Serious. But after sacrificing her comedic strengths, Heyer doesn't do enough to embrace the absurd props typical of a Gothic novel. <em>Cousin Kate</em> has murders and madness, but the book presents them with an inescapable sense of restraint and taste -- which is fatal to a Gothic novel. I want more mutilated animals, god dammit!<br /><br />But even viewed as a novel, rather than a specimen of genre, <em>Cousin Kate</em> is not a success. Nothing very much happens in the novel, so the plot must constantly regurgitate itself as protagonist Kate reviews plot points the audience still remembers from twenty pages ago. And Kate herself feels caught in traction. She begins the novel as a feisty and independent woman, but as soon as she gets to Staplewood, she begins transforming into a helpless and indecisive figure. People keep telling her to leave Staplewood, but she keeps hesitating, because if she left Staplewood, the novel would end. Reading the book feels like being stuck in limbo with Kate: she keeps discovering the same dread secrets and making the same half-hearted denials. Instead of ratcheting up the atmosphere of dread and horror, <em>Cousin Kate</em> placidly treads water.<br /><br />Torquil -- young, mercurial, and violent -- is the most interesting character in the novel, but even though Kate spends her time wringing her hands ineffectually over Torquil's sad fate, Heyer presents him with a distant and uncompassionate eye. (This is typical for Heyer novels, which you shouldn't read for their generosity of spirit.)<br /><br />So, is this the worst Heyer book I've read? Maybe. <em>Powder and Patch</em> was dire, but at least it had swashbuckling and a light heart. <em>Cousin Kate</em> is just dull. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4729615955231212535">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_160752259">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/160752259" itemprop="url" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/160752259?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 14, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2923407-katie-patchell" class="user" title="Katie Patchell">Katie Patchell</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311189.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780099490951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer160752259">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18409872061521688485">This was a good book. It was different from the other Georgette Heyer book that I read (Bath Tangle), as the second half dealt with murder and a possibly insane person. I don't read horror books, and although this had the slightly scary theme of murder, it was well-written. I enjoyed the characters and the dialogue, as well as the first half of the book. I just liked the whole Regency-Era-country-manor setting. I would suggest, though, the following:<br /><br />1. Don't read this as an introduction to the b</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18409872061521688485">This was a good book. It was different from the other Georgette Heyer book that I read (Bath Tangle), as the second half dealt with murder and a possibly insane person. I don't read horror books, and although this had the slightly scary theme of murder, it was well-written. I enjoyed the characters and the dialogue, as well as the first half of the book. I just liked the whole Regency-Era-country-manor setting. I would suggest, though, the following:<br /><br />1. Don't read this as an introduction to the books by Georgette Heyer. Start with something like Bath Tangle, or one of the others (I've heard Arabella is really good). Even though this is a good book, it's not quite like the other Regency books by her. So don't let this scare you away from her other brilliant books, if you've never read anything by her. <br /><br />2. If you have a wild imagination and get scared/tense when there's a possible murderer, or dangerous character in a book, don't read this at night. At least, don't finish it at night. It does have a good ending and plot, as well as a good romance, but it just left me wide awake.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18409872061521688485">...more</a>

          </span>

  <a href="/user/show/2411388-hannah" class="left imgcol" title="Hannah"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1272561978p2/2411388.jpg" alt="Hannah" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/91352404?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 15, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2411388-hannah" class="user" title="Hannah">Hannah</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311189.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780099490951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2411388-hannah?shelf=regencys" class="actionLinkLite">regencys</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2411388-hannah?shelf=romances" class="actionLinkLite">romances</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2411388-hannah?shelf=2010-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2010-reads</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer91352404">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1783487862370168809">I've only read 3 other Heyer books, so I can't speak with any authority on how different this offering is compared to her numerous other books, but I will note that I heard about Cousin Kate because it stirs up alot of mixed feelings (and ratings) with Heyer fans.<br /><br /><br />So of course I had to read it...<br /><br /><br />Cousin Kate starts off lighthearted, but but within 50 pages the plot takes on a darker, more gothic feel. There is a romance involved, but it's actually not the central theme of the book - mental illness</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1783487862370168809">I've only read 3 other Heyer books, so I can't speak with any authority on how different this offering is compared to her numerous other books, but I will note that I heard about Cousin Kate because it stirs up alot of mixed feelings (and ratings) with Heyer fans.<br /><br /><br />So of course I had to read it...<br /><br /><br />Cousin Kate starts off lighthearted, but but within 50 pages the plot takes on a darker, more gothic feel. There is a romance involved, but it's actually not the central theme of the book - mental illness is.<br /><br />I can see where many readers might have issues with Cousin Kate. It's certainly not a fluffy and sparkling romantic comedy. It's also not full-on gothic horror. It's a sad book in many respects, as it deals with mental illness as well as how some of the characters deal with that mental illness.<br /><br />In the end, I liked it. Didn't love it - didn't detest it. I'm certainly glad I read it, but wouldn't recommend it for a first time Heyer reader, as it doesn't really seem to fit her standard plotline formula.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1783487862370168809">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_504139151">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/504139151" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/12121311-april" class="left imgcol" title="April"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1355175719p2/12121311.jpg" alt="April" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/504139151?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 12, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/12121311-april" class="user" title="April">April</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2994583-cousin-kate" title="Hardcover " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer504139151">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12879005926170184829">I should preface my review by saying that my favorite Georgette Heyer books are the lighthearted romps populated by witty cynics (The Masqueraders is probably my favorite of these). However, there is much to recommend in Cousin Kate. As with most Heyer novels, many of the characters are well-developed, with attention to both strengths and weaknesses and excellent descriptive quality. The opening scenes of Kate's arrival at the Nidd establishment are some of the most vivid. Unfortunately, the nov</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12879005926170184829">I should preface my review by saying that my favorite Georgette Heyer books are the lighthearted romps populated by witty cynics (The Masqueraders is probably my favorite of these). However, there is much to recommend in Cousin Kate. As with most Heyer novels, many of the characters are well-developed, with attention to both strengths and weaknesses and excellent descriptive quality. The opening scenes of Kate's arrival at the Nidd establishment are some of the most vivid. Unfortunately, the novel begins to drag in the middle with the weighty effort to explore &amp; explain the psychological aspects of the characters, especially Torquil and his mother, which is rather heavy-handed. The plot developments become tedious when the reader recognizes early on that Torquil is nuttier than a box of peanut brittle and yet the characters continue to be befuddled by his behavior. The Gothic atmosphere draws some of the color from the romance at the center of it all. Philip is a bit flat and Kate changes from a sensible young woman with a roguish sense of the ridiculous into the more typical vapourish, hysterical Gothic heroine. The dramatic conclusion is entirely too tidy and the final scene disappointingly dull. However, I would still recommend the book for the colorful characters, especially Mr. Nidd, Sr. &amp; Sarah, and the finely drawn period detail.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12879005926170184829">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_15135086">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15135086" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow" class="left imgcol" title="Wealhtheow"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1178337774p2/76129.jpg" alt="Wealhtheow" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/15135086?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 12, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/76129-wealhtheow" class="user" title="Wealhtheow">Wealhtheow</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311189.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780099490951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=historical" class="actionLinkLite">historical</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/76129-wealhtheow?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer15135086">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7559546011454557782">Kate Malvern is 24 and has no relations or money. Just as she is contemplating sinking beneath the boundaries of gentility and becoming a domestic servant, her heretofore unmet aunt descends upon her. She is the Lady Broome, and she overwhelms Kate with kindess and brings her to Staplewood, the ancestral home of the Broomes. There is clearly something sinister going on at Staplewood, focused around Kate's moody cousin Torquil. Thankfully, Kate finds an ally in Philip Broome, with whom she shares</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7559546011454557782">Kate Malvern is 24 and has no relations or money. Just as she is contemplating sinking beneath the boundaries of gentility and becoming a domestic servant, her heretofore unmet aunt descends upon her. She is the Lady Broome, and she overwhelms Kate with kindess and brings her to Staplewood, the ancestral home of the Broomes. There is clearly something sinister going on at Staplewood, focused around Kate's moody cousin Torquil. Thankfully, Kate finds an ally in Philip Broome, with whom she shares spirited banter. <br />Heyer does not spend much time distinguishing Kate and Philip. They are the hero and heroine of the story, and that's that. She spends a great deal of time on Torquil, and therein lies my big disappointment. <a title=" Cousin Kate" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Cousin%20Kate"> Cousin Kate</a> begins like a light hearted romp, and ends like a light hearted romp, but in the middle everyone gives long monologues about how Torquil is <em>mad, mad I tell you</em> and the great tragedy of it all. In fact, the happy ending comes mere pages after two violent deaths, yet the victims' relatives are apparently far too pleased with the impending marriage of Philip and Kate to mourn. It's a disjointed book, and one that owes rather too much to the overwrought gothic novels of the nineteenth century. I'm also annoyed in the presentation of Torquil's madness--I read him like Colin from <a title=" The Secret Garden" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20The%20Secret%20Garden"> The Secret Garden</a>, as an under-socialized, high-strung and insensitive spoiled brat. He doesn't have trouble distinguishing reality or anything, but everyone around him takes it for granted that he needs to be institutionalized. Even the eventual deaths don't seem like proof of madness to me. I was puzzled. Didn't they have a slightly better understanding of mental illness when this was written, in the twentieth century? Torquil wasn't mad--just badly raised. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7559546011454557782">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_776836216">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/776836216" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/21428432-tweety" class="left imgcol" title="Tweety"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1415237964p2/21428432.jpg" alt="Tweety" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/776836216?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 19, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/21428432-tweety" class="user" title="Tweety">Tweety</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2224332.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780330026840" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">if you like Gothic and don't mind a slower story with a happy/sad ending </span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=gothic" class="actionLinkLite">gothic</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=england" class="actionLinkLite">england</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=sweet-and-clean-g-to-pg" class="actionLinkLite">sweet-and-clean-g-to-pg</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=georgette-heyer" class="actionLinkLite">georgette-heyer</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=grab-during-fire" class="actionLinkLite">grab-during-fire</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/21428432-tweety?shelf=owned" class="actionLinkLite">owned</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer776836216">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8428074430604272245">I do believe I am in shock. What a morbid, Ghastly, Horrid ending. I rather wish I hadn't finished it at night. <strong> <u>How on earth</u> </strong> did it end on a happy note? <br /><br />I really have to think about this review.<br /><br /><em>I've thought about it</em> <br /><br />I found it almost lyrical, I could see the beautiful still water that haunted Torquil, I felt his anguish over his dreams. His lingering worry that someone didn't have his best interests at heart. Poor Torquil.<br /><br />Minerva was so like Aunt Em from <a title="Death in Kenya by M.M. Kaye" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/732228.Death_in_Kenya">Death in Kenya</a>. They both did different</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8428074430604272245">I do believe I am in shock. What a morbid, Ghastly, Horrid ending. I rather wish I hadn't finished it at night. <strong>
  <u>How on earth</u>
</strong> did it end on a happy note? <br /><br />I really have to think about this review.<br /><br /><em>I've thought about it</em> <br /><br />I found it almost lyrical, I could see the beautiful still water that haunted Torquil, I felt his anguish over his dreams. His lingering worry that someone didn't have his best interests at heart. Poor Torquil.<br /><br />Minerva was so like Aunt Em from <a title="Death in Kenya by M.M. Kaye" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/732228.Death_in_Kenya">Death in Kenya</a>. They both did different things but their heart's were the same. That being the case I abhor Minerva. A more selfish, Obsessed, Cruel women would be hard to find. <br /><br />The suspense comes purely from mental illness, which happens to be my favorite type of suspense. I can see how the mental illness and the way it was handled pulls people in two different directions. It was mental illness down to the full moon madness. Too thrilling for words!<br /><br />I liked Philip, he wasn't often there but when he was the mood lightend. Kate was a dear even if she did think she had control of the situation.<br /><br />Kate and Torquil remind me of Valeria and Miserrimus from <a title="The Law and the Lady by Wilkie Collins" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/194649.The_Law_and_the_Lady">The Law and the Lady</a>. The personalities are similar and the conclusion for those two characters is also alike. <br /><br />Torquil is truly the strongest pull in the story, I didn't think it would make me think so much. Think of Dean in <a title="Emily Climbs (Emily, #2) by L.M. Montgomery" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/773514.Emily_Climbs__Emily___2_">Emily Climbs</a> and you will have a glimmer of what he is like. <br /><br />I loved that the characters were real to life, they lived breathed and not one of them was one dimensional. For me, this book was a treat. It's not a sparkling, witty, comedy but, a thought provoking Gothic. Though it isn't the worlds best Gothic, see <a title="Victoria Holt" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25092.Victoria_Holt">Victoria Holt</a> for those, it is a good character study. Not all the "bad" characters are wholly bad. And the good are the same, you may not be able to look up to them all, yet you can't help but like them. Beautifully haunting. <br /><br />The language was minimal. There is a horrible scene about a rabbit caught in a trap, not glorified or detailed but still nasty. And then there is a murder at the end. You don't see the murder but you see the body afterwords. Again not detailed but I have a pretty good imagination, so I could picture it all. <br /><br /><strong>
  <em>PG</em>
</strong></span>

              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer124377916">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8007391751008112446">At first I thought I'd read this before. Then I thought its familiarity was due to the usual Heyer model: impoverished orphan goes to live with estranged/distant wealthy relatives and finds them a dysfunctional family. Orphan then proceeds to solve a mystery and reconcile divided parties, marries one of them and lives happily etc, etc. But this is rather more gothic, with dark secrets, hereditary insanity, nighttime wandering along corridors, locked doors, at least one thunderstorm, and finally,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8007391751008112446">At first I thought I'd read this before. Then I thought its familiarity was due to the usual Heyer model: impoverished orphan goes to live with estranged/distant wealthy relatives and finds them a dysfunctional family. Orphan then proceeds to solve a mystery and reconcile divided parties, marries one of them and lives happily etc, etc. But this is rather more gothic, with dark secrets, hereditary insanity, nighttime wandering along corridors, locked doors, at least one thunderstorm, and finally, murder and suicide. I don't think it very effective, but then the gothic doesn't particularly appeal to me. I'm also unimpressed by Heyer's characterisation her. The heroine is of course, unusually experienced in dealing with scoundrels, having followed the drum as a child, and having earned her own living as a governess. When it comes to the villain, however, she can't see the writing on the wall...</span>

I got bogged down in the middle of this one - it's clear that Torquil is mad, it's clear that Minerva is trying to get Kate to marry him, but Heyer just fills in more and more pointless detail, perhaps in an attempt to make the Philip-Kate relationship more realistic.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText13376114422943187334">The darkest Heyer I've read, with a penniless heroine taken in by an aunt with ulterior motives, an unsympathetic hero, and a poor madman. I got bogged down in the middle of this one - it's clear that Torquil is mad, it's clear that Minerva is trying to get Kate to marry him, but Heyer just fills in more and more pointless detail, perhaps in an attempt to make the Philip-Kate relationship more realistic. She couldn't resist reverting to her regular silly tone at the end, despite the series of tragedies that complete the story, and it makes the whole book messy. Perhaps lovers of the gothic appreciate this one more than I do.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1458370422">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1458370422" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7467167-kelly" class="left imgcol" title="Kelly"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1452350638p2/7467167.jpg" alt="Kelly" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <a href="/user/show/7467167-kelly" class="user" title="Kelly">Kelly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/8270027-cousin-kate" title="Kindle Edition " class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/7467167-kelly?shelf=1800s" class="actionLinkLite">1800s</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/7467167-kelly?shelf=2015-reads" class="actionLinkLite">2015-reads</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1458370422">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16726661323442745249">So.... yeah. I liked Cousin Kate, but I didn't love it.<br /><br />Plot: Orphaned Kate (24 years old and very lovely) is dismissed from her governess position due (through no fault of her own) and returns to her old nurse, Sarah. This being a gothic novel, Kate ends up having a half-aunt (Minerva), through her father's side, and Kate's nurse writes to this aunt to inform her of owning a niece.<br /><br />The aunt sweeps in, whisks Kate off to her estate (Staplewood) while bestowing upon her expensive gowns and other gi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16726661323442745249">So.... yeah. I liked Cousin Kate, but I didn't love it.<br /><br />Plot: Orphaned Kate (24 years old and very lovely) is dismissed from her governess position due (through no fault of her own) and returns to her old nurse, Sarah. This being a gothic novel, Kate ends up having a half-aunt (Minerva), through her father's side, and Kate's nurse writes to this aunt to inform her of owning a niece.<br /><br />The aunt sweeps in, whisks Kate off to her estate (Staplewood) while bestowing upon her expensive gowns and other gifts, and is, in general, very kind to Kate. <br /><br />Once there, she discovers a cousin - the most beautiful man-child she's ever seen - 19-year-old Torquil (no, I don't know how to pronounce it). But, Torquil's behavior is excessively odd. One moment he's happy, the next moody and discussing death, suicide, and how easy it would be to kill Kate. Basically, it's how your family members greet you for the first time when you visit them, right?<br /><br />The two other main characters are Kate's uncle, Sir Timothy, and another, the barely-related cousin, Philip.<br /><br />The main gist of the story is finding out WHY Minerva invited her niece to live with them, while getting various shades on WHY Sir Timothy lives in a separate wing, and Kate and Philip falling for one another - which, naturally, is at extreme odds with Minerva's plans, and witnessing Torquil's mental illness as it manifested into frequent mood changes, extreme highs and lows. While there was no real suspense (IMO), any one of the characters could have been a victim.<br /><br />I give Heyer credit for not making Minerva evil. While her plans were rather demented, Minerva never imprisoned Kate or forced her hand into anything. I thought the ending wrapped up the story, but I wasn't completely satisfied, not the way I usually am after reading a Georgette Heyer novel. As usual, Heyer's writing is flawless, but I wasn't a huge fan of this particular story.<br /><br />Don't expect this to be your traditional Heyer regency romance, or a light-hearted romp. Cousin Kate is a straight-up gothic novel whose tone was more or less sedate.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16726661323442745249">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_975954717">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/975954717" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7290805-sheryl-tribble" class="left imgcol" title="Sheryl Tribble"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Sheryl Tribble" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/975954717?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 23, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7290805-sheryl-tribble" class="user" title="Sheryl Tribble">Sheryl Tribble</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer975954717">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer914490419207154553">Third tier Heyer. I quite like the elder Mr. Nidd, but the story is a bit of a mess; Heyer seems to have been aiming at the kind of gothic novel that was popular at the time, but she never gives the house a "personality", doesn't present the right mood, and generally doesn't have a handle on the whole concept. <br /><br />She also provides a surprisingly accurate portrayal of a form of insanity not even really defined at the time (narcissistic personality) with one character -- while at the same time presen</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText914490419207154553">Third tier Heyer. I quite like the elder Mr. Nidd, but the story is a bit of a mess; Heyer seems to have been aiming at the kind of gothic novel that was popular at the time, but she never gives the house a "personality", doesn't present the right mood, and generally doesn't have a handle on the whole concept. <br /><br />She also provides a surprisingly accurate portrayal of a form of insanity not even really defined at the time (narcissistic personality) with one character -- while at the same time presenting another character who is supposed to be insane but whose insanity fits no pattern known. I kind of suspect she was tripped up by some concept of insanity popular at the time (certainly I picked up inklings of then-current theories), but another part of me wonders if she even bothered to research that aspect. <br /><br />There are some fun bits here and there, but the uneven tone of the story can give you whiplash and the plot seems to have been deliberately developed to minimize dramatic tension, where various threats are effectively dealt with before the heroine even consciously grapples with their existence. Usually Heyer goes wrong either by being too arch or too "serious history"; it's the way she tells the story that is flawed. This book, even the plotting is inept.<br /><br />Theresa Medieros' Foreword is mostly fluff and froth and, when it comes to <em>Cousin Kate</em> itself, woefully inaccurate, but it praises a lot of what I love about Heyer and lets the newbie reader know this isn't a typical Heyer, so I'm happy with it. But I also recognize I'd have a hard time writing a foreward for this book, because it is far from Heyer's best. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="914490419207154553">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_858082822">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/858082822" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/237258-emily" class="left imgcol" title="Emily"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1357832687p2/237258.jpg" alt="Emily" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/858082822?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 17, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/237258-emily" class="user" title="Emily">Emily</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/311189.Cousin_Kate" title="Paperback 9780099490951" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/237258-emily?shelf=historicalfiction" class="actionLinkLite">historicalfiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/237258-emily?shelf=regency" class="actionLinkLite">regency</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer858082822">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4370714547467293788">Heyer wrote mostly historical romances, but also some detective/thriller novels. This is a fun mix of both, like Northanger Abbey crossed with The Turn of the Screw. Like both those stories, it features a young woman without many resources in a house that seems to have something frightening going on under the surface.<br /><br />Unlike both of those stories, the heroine is blessed with commonsense, social graces, and a decent amount of intuition. Still, her position in life leaves her vulnerable and she's w</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4370714547467293788">Heyer wrote mostly historical romances, but also some detective/thriller novels. This is a fun mix of both, like Northanger Abbey crossed with The Turn of the Screw. Like both those stories, it features a young woman without many resources in a house that seems to have something frightening going on under the surface.<br /><br />Unlike both of those stories, the heroine is blessed with commonsense, social graces, and a decent amount of intuition. Still, her position in life leaves her vulnerable and she's well aware of it. Like Hitchcock's bomb in a restaurant, the heroine's admirable qualities and growing awareness of the situation give this a nice creepy suspense that isn't common in romance novels like this. <br /><br />The psychology behind the story may be somewhat accurate to the perceptions of the time period - Heyer doesn't attempt to introduce any modern explanations, though she may imply them in the action. Still, as much as I enjoyed the way she plotted the novel, the final denouement is troubling as a "happy ending" written in a more modern era.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4370714547467293788">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1764774066797907859">2.5 stars<br /><br />Gothic attempt by Heyer. Secondary characters are fun, but Kate &amp; Phillip know each other far too briefly and interact so rarely that their marriage proposal seems odd and rushed. CRAZY evil aunt. Poor crazy son. Eeek. Hits all the Gothic notes. Fun as an example of the genre, but a far cry from Heyer's finest. It is not even all that intriguing a story apart from the Gothic trappings.<br /><br />And, yes, the aunt was very "kind' but Kate, there comes a point where you really don't owe them!</span>
