              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1071672481">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8057235142391467469">Seriously?<br /><br />The plot line is laughable and plot twists are so obvious that readers can spot them pages before they happen. My twelve year old cousin could write a better novel. More than the story line it was the portrayal of the characters that got me so mad! The most interesting one is by far the aunt, who has sacrificed her life in the pursuit of her own kind of moral and standard. She is strong-willed, has endured countless pain and suffering and has managed to survive in a barren male-dominat</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8057235142391467469">Seriously?<br /><br />The plot line is laughable and plot twists are so obvious that readers can spot them pages before they happen. My twelve year old cousin could write a better novel. More than the story line it was the portrayal of the characters that got me so mad! The most interesting one is by far the aunt, who has sacrificed her life in the pursuit of her own kind of moral and standard. She is strong-willed, has endured countless pain and suffering and has managed to survive in a barren male-dominated world by her sheer force of spirit and mind. Unfortunately all she is made out to be is a sad hag who ends up taking all the blame for EVERYTHING. Her lazy-ass husband who for years hasn't given a damn about what happened to her, hasn't supported nor her nor the son because POOR HIM he was too old to function, is made to be the sweetest and most charming of characters.<br /><br />*SPOILER*<br /><br />So they told you your son just strangled your wife but WHATEVER, let's continue to be happy and discuss the wedding plans of your nephew and the girl who you've met last week, and everyone else keeps on loving him. Why isn't ANYONE blaming him, isn't anyone disgusted at the way he is reacting? SERIOUSLY.<br /><br />*END SPOILER*<br /><br />The main characters are so stereotypical (really, the beautiful-but-broke orphan girl that has a pure soul! REALLY) the main lead Philip who is just a random good guy and has the depth of a chair. WTF. Ms. Heyer stop ripping off every half-witted romantic novel since Snow White and please write something decent.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/9801371-melissa?shelf=jane-austenish" class="actionLinkLite">jane-austenish</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/9801371-melissa?shelf=historical-romance" class="actionLinkLite">historical-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer927440975">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5092616400103617908">This is one of the few gothic novels that Georgette Heyer wrote. It was a creepy gothic read. My greatest complaint about this is that there is so much slang/cant in it that at times it was difficult to read because I wasn't sure what the characters meant. (Thank heavens for Kindle dictionary!) <br /><br />While I liked this book, it seemed like Heyer could have made it even creepier and had a more climactic ending. Instead, everything takes place off screen. It's a story with a lot of potential. There are</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5092616400103617908">This is one of the few gothic novels that Georgette Heyer wrote. It was a creepy gothic read. My greatest complaint about this is that there is so much slang/cant in it that at times it was difficult to read because I wasn't sure what the characters meant. (Thank heavens for Kindle dictionary!) <br /><br />While I liked this book, it seemed like Heyer could have made it even creepier and had a more climactic ending. Instead, everything takes place off screen. It's a story with a lot of potential. There are so many different motives by various characters and I think she could have created more tension than there was using these motivations. The heroine seems especially blind when her circumstances are obvious. The quick romance offers some light amidst all the darkness, but it is almost too good to believe. It's an interesting take on mental illness in the regency period. All in all though, it was a creepy, sad, gothic read.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3802659196543531545">Nach dem Tod ihres Vaters, der aufgrund seiner nicht standesgemäßen Ehe schon vor langer Zeit von der Familie verstoßen wurde, betätigt sich die 24-jährige Kate zunächst als Erzieherin, bevor sie von ihrer Tante auf dem Anwesen Staplewood willkommen geheißen wird. Doch auf Staplewood scheint nicht alles mit rechten Dingen zuzugehen. Liegt es wirklich am Gesundheitszustand des Hausherren, dass nie Gäste empfangen werden? Und warum ist es ihrem aufbrausenden Vetter Torquil verboten das Grundstück</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3802659196543531545">Nach dem Tod ihres Vaters, der aufgrund seiner nicht standesgemäßen Ehe schon vor langer Zeit von der Familie verstoßen wurde, betätigt sich die 24-jährige Kate zunächst als Erzieherin, bevor sie von ihrer Tante auf dem Anwesen Staplewood willkommen geheißen wird. Doch auf Staplewood scheint nicht alles mit rechten Dingen zuzugehen. Liegt es wirklich am Gesundheitszustand des Hausherren, dass nie Gäste empfangen werden? Und warum ist es ihrem aufbrausenden Vetter Torquil verboten das Grundstück zu verlassen? Welche Motive verbirgt Kates Tante hinter ihrer Freundlichkeit?<br />Dies ist wohl einer der schwächeren Georgette Heyer Romane, denn auch wenn Kate eine bewundernswert selbstständige Frau ist, fühlt sie sich ihrer Tante gegenüber doch viel zu sehr verpflichtet. Und auch das Ende hinterlässt einen etwas schalen Beigeschmack, hat man doch das Gefühl, dass sich all der unschönen Elemente noch schnell entledigt wird, um das Happy End herbeizuführen.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sCujwgbGNBOv0HH4RQZBpZSHcf/EY7GjDX56tfktg8zV/5wR9BQg6SMIBUM7Z6cX3XCy5o2+9glnd38nNbh1iQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Z7oB9xjNzNwVGnIxLaPzyN6Tcu4RWSmbSfG7+1UrEssCbj4k6h/YJpnCBopTwhV6l2Sx91iEbjEj+L5pmb7kjg==')})
  }

Lord Bevis presses his suit with Lady Elizabeth, until she agrees, at long last, to marry him. Clanross proclaims his pride in her accomplishment, but Lord Bevis\'s reaction is far more traditional. Willoughby introduces a beautiful woman into the mix and the twins further complicate it.             if ($('bookCover_2908100').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_2908100').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]&gt;
</script>
</li>
</ul>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer">About Georgette Heyer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/18067.Georgette_Heyer"><img alt="18067" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1336748892p2/18067.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer17026726049982402064">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Hey</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17026726049982402064">Georgette Heyer was a prolific historical romance and detective fiction novelist. Her writing career began in 1921, when she turned a story for her younger brother into the novel <a title=" The Black Moth" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/311322._The_Black_Moth"> The Black Moth</a>.<br /><br />In 1925 she married George Ronald Rougier, a mining engineer, and he often provided basic plot outlines for her thrillers. Beginning in 1932, Heyer released one romance novel and one thriller each year.<br /><br />Heyer was an intensely private person who remained a best selling author all her life without the aid of publicity. She made no appearances, never gave an interview and only answered fan letters herself if they made an interesting historical point. She sometimes wrote under the pseudonym Stella Martin.<br /><br />Her Regencies were inspired by <a title=" Jane Austen" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1265._Jane_Austen"> Jane Austen</a>, but unlike Austen, who wrote about and for the times in which she lived, Heyer was forced to include copious information about the period so that her readers would understand the setting. While some critics thought her novels were too detailed, others considered the level of detail to be Heyer's greatest asset.<br /><br />Heyer remains a popular and much-loved author, known for essentially establishing the historical romance genre and its subgenre Regency romance.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17026726049982402064">...more</a>

    </div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/2230129-cousin-kate">Quotes from Cousin Kate</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div tyle="padding-bottom:15px" class="stacked">
            <span class="readable">“Has it occurred to you, Kate, that she is placing you under an obligation?"<br /><br />"Oh, yes, indeed it has, and it is crushing me!" she said earnestly. "If only there were some way of requiting her - not arranging flowers, or entertaining Sir Timothy, or bearing Torquil company, but a big thing! Something that was vital to her, or - or even something that entailed a sacrifice! But there isn't anything that I can discover."<br /><br />There was a pause, during which he frowned down at his well-kept finger-nails. At length he said slowly: "If she were to demand it of you, would you be prepared to make a sacrifice of yourself?”</span>
            <nobr>
              —
              <a href="/quotes/309890-has-it-occurred-to-you-kate-that-she-is-placing" class="actionLinkLite">4 likes</a>
            </nobr>
            <div class="clear"></div>
          </div>
